<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_di2832_1_9"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2>
Kraft Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are
unaudited. It is the opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of
a normal recurring nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, and management's discussion and analysis of financial condition and results of
operations, which appear in the Company's Annual Report to Shareholders and which are incorporated by reference into the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. The Company's new segments are U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S.
Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America
reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously
reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America and Asia Pacific segment. Also, in connection with the new global organizational structure, Kraft, in
March&nbsp;2004, changed the legal name of one of its subsidiaries, Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc., to Kraft Foods Global,&nbsp;Inc. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Certain
prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform with the current year's presentation, due primarily to the new global organizational structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS")
No.&nbsp;123, "Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which does not result in compensation cost for stock options. The market value at date of grant of restricted stock and rights to receive
shares of stock is recorded as compensation expense over the period of restriction. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004 and 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock to eligible employees, giving them in most instances all of the rights
of shareholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber the shares and rights. The shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if certain employment conditions are not
met. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S. based employees and also issued to eligible non-U.S. employees
rights to receive approximately 1.9&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on most of the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2007. The market value per restricted
share or right was $32.23 on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded
compensation expense related to restricted stock and rights of $25&nbsp;million and $11&nbsp;million for the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 and March&nbsp;31, 2003, respectively. The
unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was $294&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>9</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Asset Impairment and Exit Costs:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and
lowering its cost structure, and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the
elimination of approximately six thousand positions. Over the next three years, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals,
severance and other implementation costs, including an estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are
expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, pre-tax charges under the restructuring program of $279&nbsp;million were recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated
statement of earnings. These charges resulted from the first quarter 2004 announcement of the closing of five plants, the termination of a co-manufacturing agreement and the commencement
of a number of workforce reduction programs. Approximately $88&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges will result in cash payments. Pre-tax restructuring liability activity for
the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first quarter of 2004, as part of
the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,000 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings. Other costs
incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of a co-manufacturing agreement. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, during the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash
pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States and certain brands in Mexico. This charge was recorded as asset impairment
and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
pre-tax asset impairment and exit costs, which totaled $308&nbsp;million for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2004, were included in the operating companies income of the
following segments: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At March&nbsp;31, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. owned approximately 84.6% of the Company's outstanding shares of capital stock. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s subsidiary,
Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc., provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary,
corporate affairs, information technology and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a
management fee, were $73&nbsp;million and $83&nbsp;million for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 and 2003, respectively. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company had short-term amounts payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. of $384&nbsp;million. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London
Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of
damages are sought. While the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the
Company's consolidated financial position or results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At March&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture activities, approximated
$27&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2013, with $4&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2005. The Company is required to perform under these guarantees
in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has a liability of $20&nbsp;million on its condensed consolidated balance sheet at
March&nbsp;31, 2004, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=13,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=308510,FOLIO='13',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DI2832A.;16',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_di2832_1_14"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;8.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company manufactures and markets packaged retail food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products
through Kraft Foods Global,&nbsp;Inc. and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and Kraft International Commercial.
Reportable segments for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are organized and managed by geographic
location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.
Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. The
Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of
segment profitability reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Segment
data were as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Benefit Plans:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In December&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued a revised SFAS No.&nbsp;132, "Employers' Disclosures about Pensions and Other Postretirement
Benefits." In the first quarter of 2004, the Company adopted the new interim-period disclosure requirements of this pronouncement relating to net periodic benefit cost and employer contributions to
benefit plans, except for certain interim-period disclosures about non-U.S. plans which are not required until after December&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company sponsors noncontributory defined benefit pension plans covering substantially all U.S. employees. Pension coverage for employees of the Company's non-U.S. subsidiaries is
provided, to the extent deemed appropriate, through separate plans, many of which are governed by local statutory requirements. In addition, the Company's U.S. and Canadian subsidiaries provide health
care and other benefits to substantially all retired employees. Health care benefits for retirees outside the United States and Canada are generally covered through local government plans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Employer Contributions  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company presently plans to make contributions, to the extent that they are tax deductible, in order to maintain plan assets in excess of the accumulated benefit obligation
of its U.S. funded plans. In April&nbsp;2004, $60&nbsp;million of employer contributions were made to U.S. plans. Currently, the Company anticipates making additional contributions of
approximately $230&nbsp;million during the remainder of 2004, based on current tax law. Contributions were previously estimated to be $70&nbsp;million for the full year. However, this estimate is
subject to change due primarily to asset performance significantly different than the assumed long-term rate of return on pension assets and significant changes in interest rates. During
the first quarter of 2004, pension plan contributions were $84&nbsp;million, related principally to non-U.S. plans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the United States enacted into law the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization Act of 2003 (the "Act"). The Act establishes a prescription drug benefit under
Medicare, </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>18</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>known
as "Medicare Part&nbsp;D," and a federal subsidy to sponsors of retiree health care benefit plans that provide a benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position No.&nbsp;106-1, "Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and
Modernization Act of 2003" ("FSP&nbsp;106-1"). The Company has elected to defer accounting for the effects of the Act, as permitted by FSP&nbsp;106-1. Therefore, in
accordance with FSP&nbsp;106-1, the Company's accumulated postretirement benefit obligation and net postretirement health care costs included in the condensed
consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes do not reflect the favorable effects of the Act on the plans. Specific authoritative guidance on the accounting for the federal subsidy is
pending, and that guidance, when issued, could require the Company to change previously reported information. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Description of the Company  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in
the United States. At March&nbsp;31, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 97.9% of the combined voting power of Kraft's outstanding capital stock and owned approximately 84.6% of the outstanding
shares of Kraft's capital stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged retail food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
Global,&nbsp;Inc. (formerly known as Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc.) and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and
Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are
organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Executive Summary  </B></FONT></P>

March&nbsp;31, 2004 from the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2003 were due primarily to the following (in&nbsp;millions, except per share data): </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
unfavorable impact of asset impairment and exit costs on net earnings and diluted EPS is due to the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a multi-year restructuring program. As part of this program,
the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. Over the next three years, the Company expects to incur up to
$1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, including an estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company recorded
pre-tax charges of $279&nbsp;million for this program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Intangible Asset Impairment Charge</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;During the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of its goodwill and intangible
assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States
and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective tax rate decreased by 3.2&nbsp;percentage points to 31.9%, reflecting the reversal of tax provisions that are no longer required due to tax events that occurred
during the first quarter of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
favorable currency impact on net earnings and diluted EPS is due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar versus the euro and the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
decrease in results from operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial reflecting higher commodity and benefit costs and increased promotional spending.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial reflecting higher costs, including benefits, commodities and infrastructure investment in developing markets. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>2004 Projected Results</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In April&nbsp;2004, the Company announced that it expects 2004 full-year diluted EPS at the lower end
of the Company's previously issued guidance of $1.63 to $1.70, due primarily to higher than originally anticipated commodity costs, particularly cheese. Cheese costs, which have recently reached
historical highs, are expected to moderate through the remainder of the year. The projected 2004 EPS includes anticipated charges of $0.30 from asset impairment and exit costs. The projected diluted
EPS also reflects an overall lower tax rate for the year, which is expected to result from the final resolution of certain U.S. and foreign tax matters. The factors described in the section entitled </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Forward-Looking and
Cautionary Statements</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> of the following Discussion and Analysis represent continuing risks to this projection. </FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_dm2832_1_22"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Discussion and Analysis  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company is subject to a number of challenges that may adversely affect its businesses. These challenges, which are discussed below and under the "Forward-Looking and
Cautionary Statements," include: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>fluctuations
in commodity prices;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>movements
of foreign currencies against the U.S. dollar;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitive
challenges in various products and markets, including price gaps with competitor products and the increasing price-consciousness of consumers;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
rising cost environment;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
trend toward increasing consolidation in the retail trade and consequent inventory reductions;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>changing
consumer preferences, including low-carbohydrate diet trends;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitors
with different profit objectives and less susceptibility to currency exchange rates; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>consumer
concerns about food safety, quality and health, including concerns about genetically modified organisms, trans-fatty acids and obesity. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>To
confront these challenges, the Company continues to take steps to build the value of its brands, to improve its food business portfolio with new product and marketing initiatives, to reduce costs
through productivity and to address consumer concerns about food safety, quality and health. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced its adoption of a four-point plan to achieve sustainable growth. The first element of the plan is to build brand value by continuing to
improve its products, to use more value-added packaging, to develop innovative new products, to manage price gaps effectively and to build closer relationships with consumers. The Company anticipates
$500 to $600&nbsp;million of increased spending in 2004 over 2003 to manage price gaps, to increase media presence, to drive growth in developing markets and non-measured channels, to
enhance brand equity and to support new products. In the first quarter of 2004, the Company increased its marketing investment by approximately $75&nbsp;million versus the first quarter of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
second element of the plan is to accelerate the shift in the Company's brand portfolio to address growing consumer demand including products to meet their health and wellness concerns and their
desire for convenience. The Company is reducing trans-fat in its products, identifying its products that are low in carbohydrates, introducing more sugar-free products, and
emphasizing positive nutrition products. The Company is addressing convenience needs by offering more convenient packaging, such as single-serve and resealable packaging, and products requiring
reduced preparation. The Company is also offering packaging that is customized to suit the needs of growing alternate channels of distribution such as supercenters, mass merchandisers, drugstores and
club stores. The Company also plans to shift its portfolio to reflect changing demographics, for example, by expanding the availability of Hispanic products and bilingual packaging. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
third component of the plan is to expand the Company's global scale through international growth, particularly in developing markets. These markets account for approximately 84% of the world's
population and 30% of its packaged food consumption, but only 11% of the Company's 2003 net revenues. The plan calls </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>22</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=22,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=332858,FOLIO='22',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DM2832A.;13',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_dm2832_1_23"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>for
the Company to capture the growth potential of its core categories in markets where it has operations and to expand its core categories into new markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
the final component of its plan, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost
structure, and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions.
Over the next three years, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including an
estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company recorded $308&nbsp;million of asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. These pre-tax charges
were composed of $279&nbsp;million of costs under the restructuring program and $29&nbsp;million of impairment charges relating to intangible assets. Costs under the restructuring program resulted
from the first quarter 2004 announcement of the closing of five plants, the termination of a co-manufacturing agreement and the commencement of a number of workforce reduction programs.
Approximately $88&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges will result in cash payments. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company also completed its annual review of goodwill and
intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the
United States and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pre-tax
restructuring liability activity for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first quarter of 2004, as part of
the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,000 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings. Other costs
incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of a co-manufacturing agreement. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, the Company expects to spend approximately $140&nbsp;million in capital over the next three years to implement the restructuring program, including approximately $50&nbsp;million in
2004. Cost savings as a result of the restructuring program are expected to be approximately $120&nbsp;million to $140&nbsp;million in 2004, and are anticipated to reach approximately
$400&nbsp;million by 2006, all of which are expected to be used in supporting brand-building initiatives. Cost savings during the first quarter were approximately $10&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility and intensive price competition, and can influence consumer and trade buying patterns. The Company's businesses are subject to
fluctuating commodity costs, including dairy, coffee and cocoa costs. In the first quarter of 2004, the Company's commodity costs on average have been higher than those incurred in 2003, most notably
dairy, soybean oil, grains and coffee. Dairy costs in particular are expected to remain significantly higher in 2004 than in 2003 because of lower U.S. milk supplies. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Note
that in the ordinary course of business, the Company is subject to many influences that can impact the timing of sales to customers, including the timing of holidays and other annual or special
events, seasonality of </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>23</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=23,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=632292,FOLIO='23',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DM2832A.;13',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_dm2832_1_24"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>certain
products, significant weather conditions, timing of Company and customer incentive programs, customer inventory reduction programs, Company initiatives to improve supply chain efficiency,
including efforts to align product shipments more closely with consumption by shifting some of its customer marketing programs to a consumption based approach, financial situations of customers and
general economic conditions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the first quarter of 2004 and 2003, total purchases of businesses, net of acquired cash, were
$119&nbsp;million and $5&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2003, the Company had operations and plants or sold products to third-party distributors located in 15&nbsp;Middle East countries (as defined by the U.S. Department of State, Bureau of Near
Eastern Affairs), including a biscuit business acquired during 2003 in Egypt. In the region, the Company had operations and plants in three countries (Egypt, Morocco and, through a majority owned
joint venture, Saudi Arabia). In addition, the Company sold products to third-party distributors located in 12 of these countries (Algeria, Bahrain, Israel, Jordan, Kuwait, Lebanon, Oman, Qatar,
Syria, Tunisia, United Arab Emirates and Yemen). Revenue generated from operations or sales to the third-party distributors in the Middle East was approximately $230&nbsp;million in 2003
representing 3.3% of the net revenue of the Europe, Middle East and Africa segment. In 2004, the Company continues to conduct business in these countries, except for Syria, where the Company ceased
sales to the third-party distributor early in the year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2003, the Company was advised by the Fort Worth District Office of the Securities and Exchange Commission ("SEC") that the staff is considering recommending that the SEC bring a
civil injunctive action against the Company charging it with aiding and abetting Fleming Companies ("Fleming") in violations of the securities laws. District staff alleges that a Company employee, who
received a similar notice, signed documents requested by Fleming, which Fleming used in order to accelerate its revenue recognition. The notice does not contain any allegations or statements regarding
the Company's accounting for transactions with Fleming. The Company believes that it properly recorded the transactions in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United
States. The Company has submitted a response to the staff indicating why it believes that no enforcement action should be brought against it. The Company is cooperating fully with the SEC with respect
to this matter and the SEC's investigation of Fleming. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;8. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general
corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the
business performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Three Months Ended March&nbsp;31, 2004  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 with the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 0.5%, due primarily to acquisitions and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment, partially offset by the impact of divested
businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $334&nbsp;million (4.5%), due primarily to favorable currency ($306&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($45&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions
($12&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses ($31&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income decreased $499&nbsp;million (33.5%), due primarily to pre-tax charges in 2004 for asset impairment and exit costs ($308&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher
pricing ($134&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher marketing, administrative and research costs ($58&nbsp;million) and higher fixed
manufacturing costs ($33&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by favorable currency ($35&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($8&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $306&nbsp;million and operating income by $35&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and
the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=6,SEQ=25,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=399597,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DM2832A.;13',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_dm2832_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $14&nbsp;million, due primarily to lower average debt outstanding. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective tax rate decreased by 3.2&nbsp;percentage points to 31.9%, reflecting the reversal of tax provisions that are no longer required due to tax events that occurred
during the first quarter of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $560&nbsp;million decreased $288&nbsp;million (34.0%), due primarily to lower operating income, partially offset by a lower effective tax rate. Diluted and basic EPS, which were
both $0.33, decreased by 32.7%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 1.0%, due primarily to increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment, partially offset by a decline in the U.S. Convenient Meals segment
and the U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $133&nbsp;million (2.5%), due primarily to favorable currency ($72&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($58&nbsp;million). Higher pricing, reflecting commodity-driven
pricing in foodservice was substantially offset by increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $427&nbsp;million (33.5%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exits costs ($262&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs,
net of higher pricing ($125&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($27 </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=7,SEQ=26,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=172178,FOLIO='26',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DM2832A.;13',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_dm2832_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>million,
including higher benefit costs) and higher marketing, administration and research costs ($31&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable currency ($11&nbsp;million) and higher
volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.3%, due primarily to a decline in cereals and beverages, partially offset by gains in desserts, enhancers and coffee.
In cereals, volume declined driven by category weakness, the timing of new product introductions and increased competitive activity. Beverages volume also declined, due to the timing of new product
introductions and related trade inventory reductions. In desserts, volume increased, due primarily to higher shipments of sugar-free, ready-to-eat desserts and
frozen toppings. Volume also increased in enhancers, primarily salad dressings and mayonnaise, and in coffee due to strong performance in supercenters. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $11&nbsp;million (0.7%), due to lower volume/mix ($22&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $62&nbsp;million (11.9%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of lower promotional spending ($26&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs), the 2004
pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($15&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($12&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($8&nbsp;million) and
higher benefit costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> U.S. Snacks.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume was equal to the prior year, as higher salted snacks volume was offset by lower biscuits volume. Salted snacks volume increased due to consumer
nutrition trends and marketing programs in nuts. In biscuits, volume declined, as consumer health and wellness concerns continued to affect consumption. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $21&nbsp;million (1.8%), due to unfavorable volume/mix ($22&nbsp;million) and higher promotional spending, partially offset by higher pricing and reduced product returns. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $230&nbsp;million, due to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($176&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs ($20&nbsp;million,
driven by higher commodity costs, partially offset by reduced product returns), unfavorable volume/mix ($15&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($13&nbsp;million)
and higher fixed manufacturing costs ($6&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.9%, due primarily to higher volume in foodservice and cheese. Volume in the foodservice
business increased, due primarily to higher shipments to national accounts. In cheese, volume also increased, benefiting from increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $158&nbsp;million (10.1%), due to higher volume/mix ($93&nbsp;million), favorable currency ($72&nbsp;million) and higher foodservice pricing, partially offset by higher
promotional reinvestment spending in cheese. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $107&nbsp;million (34.1%), due to unfavorable costs ($66&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), the 2004
pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($62&nbsp;million), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($15&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and higher marketing,
administration and research costs, partially offset by higher volume/mix ($33&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($11&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> U.S. Convenient Meals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.9%, due primarily to lower shipments in meals, partially offset by gains in meats. In meals, volume declined due to the
discontinuation of certain product lines in the second half of 2003. Meats volume increased driven by higher consumption of cold cuts, supported by higher investment spending. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $7&nbsp;million (0.7%), due primarily to favorable volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
decreased 0.9%, due primarily to the impact of the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, and price competition and trade inventory reductions in
several markets, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $201&nbsp;million (9.6%), due to favorable currency ($234&nbsp;million), the impact of acquisitions ($11&nbsp;million) and higher pricing (reflecting devaluation-driven
cost increases in Latin America), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($31&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($13&nbsp;million) and increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $70&nbsp;million (26.8%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($46&nbsp;million), higher marketing,
administration and research costs ($27&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs and infrastructure investment in developing markets), unfavorable costs ($15&nbsp;million, including commodities
and fixed manufacturing costs) and the impact of divestitures, partially offset by favorable currency ($24&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 1.8%, due primarily to the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in
2003, price competition in France and trade inventory reductions in Russia, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions and volume growth in Germany and the United Kingdom. Beverages volume
declined, driven by price competition on coffee in France and lower consumption of refreshment beverages in the Middle East, partially offset by higher coffee volume in Germany and Spain. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=28,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=829854,FOLIO='28',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DO2832A.;11',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_do2832_1_29"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Cheese
volume also declined, impacted by the divestiture of a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, partially offset by increased cream cheese shipments in the United Kingdom and Germany.
Convenient meals volume declined, impacted by the divestiture of a rice business in Europe in 2003. In grocery, volume increased, benefiting from gains in the United Kingdom and Egypt. Snacks volume
also increased, as gains in biscuits, benefiting from acquisitions, and new confectionery product introductions in Germany, Austria and Spain were partially offset by confectionery price competition
and trade inventory reductions in Russia. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $167&nbsp;million (10.7%), due to favorable currency ($208&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($11&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures
($31&nbsp;million), lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($14&nbsp;million) and lower volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $38&nbsp;million (19.4%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($32&nbsp;million), higher marketing,
administration and research costs ($21&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs as well as infrastructure investment in eastern Europe), the impact of divestitures ($5&nbsp;million), lower
pricing and higher promotional spending, partially offset by favorable currency ($26&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.4%, due primarily to gains in Argentina, Brazil, Venezuela and China, partially offset by declines in
Puerto Rico, Australia and Southeast Asia, due to price competition. Snacks volume increased in Argentina, Brazil and China, aided by new product introductions, and growth in Venezuela, due to the
2003 national strike. Cheese and grocery volume also increased, due primarily to gains in Venezuela. Beverages volume declined, impacted by price competition in Puerto Rico and Mexico, partially
offset by gains in China, benefiting from marketing programs in refreshment beverages. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $34&nbsp;million (6.3%), due to favorable currency ($26&nbsp;million) and higher pricing ($14&nbsp;million, reflecting devaluation-driven cost increases), partially offset
by unfavorable volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $32&nbsp;million (49.2%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($14&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net
of higher pricing ($9&nbsp;million) and higher marketing, administration and research costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Financial Review</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by Operating Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, net cash provided by operating activities was $494&nbsp;million compared with $315&nbsp;million in the comparable 2003 period. The increase in net cash provided
by operating activities is due primarily to a lower use of cash to fund working capital, primarily receivables (timing of shipments) and inventory, reflecting ongoing company efforts to reduce
inventory levels. Partially offsetting these items is a reduction in taxes payable, reflecting the impact of lower operating income. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in Investing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly investigating
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses that are outside its core categories or that do not meet its growth or profitability targets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, net cash used in investing activities was $266&nbsp;million, compared with $222&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2003. This increase primarily reflects higher
purchases of businesses, partially offset by lower capital expenditures. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S. based beverage business. Capital expenditures for the first
quarter of 2004 were $148&nbsp;million, compared with $220&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2003. The Company continues to expect full-year capital expenditures to be at or </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>29</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=29,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=42351,FOLIO='29',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DO2832A.;11',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_do2832_1_30"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>slightly
above full-year 2003 expenditures of $1.1&nbsp;billion, including capital expenditures required for the restructuring program announced in January&nbsp;2004. These
expenditures are expected to be funded from operations. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in Financing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, net cash used in financing activities was $471&nbsp;million, compared with $140&nbsp;million during the first quarter of 2003. The increase in net cash used in
financing activities is due primarily to the net movement in debt (including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates), an increase in the Company's Class&nbsp;A share repurchases and
an increase in dividend payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Debt
and Liquidity</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Debt.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company's total debt, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, was $13.5&nbsp;billion at March&nbsp;31, 2004 and
December&nbsp;31, 2003. The Company's debt-to-equity ratio was 0.47 at March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003. The Company's
debt-to-capitalization ratio was 0.32 at March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had short-term amounts payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. of $384&nbsp;million and $543&nbsp;million, respectively.
Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
March&nbsp;2004, the Company filed a Form&nbsp;S-3 shelf registration statement with the SEC, under which the Company may sell debt securities and/or warrants to purchase debt
securities in one or more offerings up to a total amount of $4.0&nbsp;billion, when the Form&nbsp;S-3 filing becomes effective. The prospectus contained in the registration statement
is a combined prospectus which also covers an additional $250&nbsp;million of unissued principal amount under the previous Form&nbsp;S-3 shelf registration statement filed with the SEC
in April&nbsp;2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Credit Lines.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company maintains revolving credit facilities that have historically been used to support the issuance of commercial paper. At March&nbsp;31,

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's revolving credit facilities, which are for its sole use, require the maintenance of a minimum net worth of $18.2&nbsp;billion. The Company met this covenant at March&nbsp;31, 2004
and expects to continue to meet this covenant. The foregoing revolving credit facilities do not include any other financial tests, any credit rating triggers or any provisions that could require the
posting of collateral. The multi-year revolving credit facility enables the Company to reclassify short-term debt on a long-term basis. At March&nbsp;31, 2004,
$2.0&nbsp;billion of commercial paper borrowings that the Company intends to refinance were reclassified as long-term debt. The Company expects to continue to refinance
long-term and short-term debt from time to time. The nature and amount of the Company's long-term and short-term debt and the proportionate amount of
each can be expected to vary as a result of future business requirements, market conditions and other factors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to the above, certain international subsidiaries of Kraft maintain uncommitted credit lines to meet the short-term working capital needs of the international businesses. These
credit lines, which amounted to </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Guarantees.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As discussed in Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company had third-party guarantees, which are
primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture activities, of approximately $27&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2004. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2013, with
$4&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2005. The Company is required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve
performance measures. The Company has a liability of $20&nbsp;million on its condensed consolidated balance sheet at March&nbsp;31, 2004, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, at March&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company was contingently liable for $103&nbsp;million of guarantees related to its own performance. These include surety bonds related to dairy commodity
purchases and guarantees related to the payment of custom duties and taxes, and letters of credit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Guarantees
do not have, and are not expected to have, a significant impact on the Company's liquidity. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company believes that its cash from operations and existing credit facilities will provide sufficient liquidity to meet its working capital needs, planned capital expenditures, future contractual
obligations and payment of its anticipated quarterly dividends. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Equity
and Dividends</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
repurchased 4.9&nbsp;million shares of its Class&nbsp;A common stock during the first quarter of 2004 at a cost of $163&nbsp;million. At March&nbsp;31, 2004, cumulative repurchases under
its previously announced $700&nbsp;million authority totaled 6.5&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock at an aggregate cost of $213&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;1. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Accounting Policies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, during the first quarter of 2004, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million
Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S. based employees and also issued to eligible non-U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.9&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares.
Restrictions on most of the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2007. The market value per restricted share or right was $32.23 on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Dividends
paid in the first quarter of 2004 and 2003 were $309&nbsp;million and $259&nbsp;million, respectively, an increase of 19.3%, reflecting a 20.0% higher dividend rate in 2004, partially
offset by a lower number of shares outstanding as a result of Class&nbsp;A share repurchases. The present annualized dividend rate is $0.72 per common share. The declaration of dividends is subject
to the discretion of Kraft's Board of Directors and will depend on various factors, including the Company's net earnings, financial condition, cash requirements, future prospects and other factors
deemed relevant by Kraft's Board of Directors. </FONT></P>

<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=31,EFW="2135826",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=624624,FOLIO='31',FILE='DISK043:[04CHI2.04CHI2832]DO2832A.;11',USER='DINGRAM',CD='10-MAY-2004;11:21' -->
<A NAME="page_do2832_1_32"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Market Risk</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company operates globally, with manufacturing and sales facilities in various locations around the world, and utilizes certain financial instruments to manage its foreign
currency and commodity exposures, which primarily relate to forecasted transactions. Derivative financial instruments are used by the Company, principally to reduce exposures to market risks resulting
from fluctuations in foreign exchange rates and commodity prices by creating offsetting exposures. The Company is not a party to leveraged derivatives and, by policy, does not use financial
instruments for speculative purposes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Substantially
all of the Company's derivative financial instruments are effective as hedges. During the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2004 and 2003, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges
was not material. At March&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company was hedging forecasted transactions for periods not exceeding fifteen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other
comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Foreign exchange rates.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company uses forward foreign exchange contracts and foreign currency options to mitigate its exposure to changes in foreign currency
exchange rates from third-party and intercompany forecasted transactions. The primary currencies to which the Company is exposed, based on the size and location of its businesses, include the euro,
Swiss franc, British pound and Canadian dollar. At March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had foreign exchange option and forward contracts with aggregate notional amounts of
$2,475&nbsp;million and $2,486&nbsp;million, respectively. The effective portion of unrealized gains and losses associated with forward contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other
comprehensive earnings (losses) until the underlying hedged transactions are reported on the Company's consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Commodities.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is exposed to price risk related to forecasted purchases of certain commodities used as raw materials by the Company's businesses.
Accordingly, the Company uses commodity forward contracts as cash flow hedges, primarily for coffee, cocoa, milk and cheese. Commodity futures and options are also used to hedge the price of certain
commodities, including milk, coffee, cocoa, wheat, corn, sugar and soybean oil. In general, commodity forward contracts qualify for the normal purchase exception under Statement of Financial
Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;133 and are, therefore, not subject to the provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;133. At March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had net long
commodity positions of $144&nbsp;million and $255&nbsp;million, respectively. Unrealized gains or losses on net commodity positions were immaterial at March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31,
2003. The effective portion of unrealized gains and losses on commodity futures and option contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) and is recognized
as a component of cost of sales in the Company's consolidated statement of earnings when the related inventory is sold. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Contingencies</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>See Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and Part&nbsp;II&#151;Other Information, Item 1.&nbsp;Legal Proceedings for a
discussion of contingencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The Company and its representatives may from time to time make written or oral forward-looking statements, including statements contained in the Company's filings with the
Securities and Exchange Commission ("SEC"), in its reports to shareholders and in press releases and investor webcasts. One can identify these forward-looking statements by use of words such as
"strategy," "expects," "plans," "anticipates," "believes," "will," "continues," "estimates," "intends," "projects," "goals," "targets" and other words of similar meaning. One can also identify them by
the fact that they do not relate strictly to historical or current facts. These statements are based on our assumptions and estimates and are subject to risks and uncertainties. In connection with the
"safe harbor" provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995, the Company is hereby identifying important factors that could cause actual results and outcomes to differ materially
from those contained in any forward-looking statement made by or on behalf of the Company; any such statement is qualified by reference to the following cautionary statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Each
of the Company's segments is subject to intense competition, changes in consumer preferences and demand for its products, including low-carbohydrate diet trends, the effects of changing prices
for its raw materials and local economic and market conditions. Their results are dependent upon their continued ability to promote brand equity successfully, to anticipate and respond to new consumer
trends, to develop new products and markets, to broaden brand portfolios, to compete effectively with lower priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels and to
improve productivity. The Company's results are also dependent on its ability to consummate and successfully integrate acquisitions and to realize the cost savings and improved asset utilization
contemplated by its restructuring program. In addition, the Company is subject to the effects of foreign economies, currency movements, fluctuations in levels of customer inventories and credit and
other business risks related to its customers operating in a challenging economic and competitive environment. The Company's results are affected by its access to credit markets, borrowing costs and
credit ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. The Company's benefit expense is subject to the investment performance of pension plan assets,
interest rates and cost increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The Company's assessment of the fair value of its operations for purposes of assessing impairment of goodwill
and intangibles is based on discounting projections of future cash flows and is affected by the interest rate market and general economic and market conditions. The food industry continues to be
subject to recalls if products become adulterated or misbranded, liability if product consumption causes injury, ingredient disclosure and labeling laws and regulations and the possibility that
consumers could lose confidence in the safety and quality of certain food products. The food industry is also subject to consumer concerns regarding genetically modified organisms and the health
implications of obesity and trans-fatty acids. Developments in any of these areas, which are more fully described elsewhere in this document and which descriptions are incorporated into this section
by reference, could cause the Company's results to differ materially from results that have been or may be projected by or on behalf of the Company. The Company cautions that the foregoing list of
important factors is not exclusive. Any forward-looking statements are made as of the date of the document in which they appear. The Company does not
undertake to update any forward-looking statement that may be made from time to time by or on behalf of the Company. </FONT></P>

Company carried out an evaluation, with the participation of the Company's management, including the Company's Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the

<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
The Company is party to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including the matters discussed below. While the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome
of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
On January&nbsp;2, 2004, the Canada Border Services Agency ("CBSA"), an agency of the Canadian government, announced the initiation of an investigation into an allegation of injurious dumping by Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFNA") of frozen
self-rising crust pizza from the United States following a complaint filed by McCain Foods Limited, which claims that the alleged dumping is materially injuring Canadian production by causing price erosion, price suppression, lost sales and reduced
profits. Kraft Canada is the major importer of frozen self-rising crust pizza from the United States, which it sells under the brand name </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Delissio</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>. On the basis of McCain's allegation, the Canadian
International Trade Tribunal ("CITT") issued a preliminary finding that there was a reasonable indication of injury in the Canadian market. Following this finding, the CBSA must make a preliminary determination as to whether dumping has occurred.
This is currently scheduled for not later than May&nbsp;17, 2004. If the CBSA were to conclude on a preliminary basis that dumping has occurred, the CITT would commence a formal inquiry into whether the imports are in fact materially injuring
Canadian production. The CITT would be required to hold hearings and make a final determination as to material injury, if any, by the end of August&nbsp;2004. The Company is vigorously contesting McCain's allegations of dumping and material injury.
If material injury is found by the CITT, dumping duties will be assessed against imports of frozen self-rising crust pizza from the United States for an initial period of five years. The dumping duties will be based upon a comparison of normal values
determined by the CBSA for KFNA against KFNA's export prices. Frozen pizzas are currently imported into Canada from the United States on a duty-free basis under the terms of the North American Free Trade Agreement.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
In November&nbsp;2003, the Company was advised by the Fort Worth District Office of the Securities and Exchange Commission ("SEC") that the staff is considering recommending that the SEC bring a civil injunctive action against the Company charging it
with aiding and abetting Fleming Companies ("Fleming") in violations of the securities laws. District staff alleges that a Company employee, who received a similar notice, signed documents requested by Fleming, which Fleming used in order to
accelerate its revenue recognition. The notice does not contain any allegations or statements regarding the Company's accounting for transactions with Fleming. The Company believes that it properly recorded the transactions in accordance with
accounting principles generally accepted in the United States. The Company has submitted a response to the staff indicating why it believes that no enforcement action should be brought against it. The Company is cooperating fully with the SEC with
respect to this matter and the SEC's investigation of Fleming.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
In October&nbsp;2002, Mr.&nbsp;Mustapha Gaouar filed suit in the Commercial Court of Casablanca against the Company and Mr.&nbsp;Omar Berrada claiming damages of approximately $31&nbsp;million arising from a non-compete undertaking signed by
Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar allegedly under duress. The non-compete clause&nbsp;was contained in an agreement concluded in 1986 between Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar and Mr.&nbsp;Berrada acting for himself and for his group of companies, including Les Cafes Ennasr (renamed
Kraft Foods Maroc), which was acquired by the Company from Mr.&nbsp;Berrada in 2001. In June&nbsp;2003, the court issued a preliminary judgment against Kraft Foods Maroc and Mr.&nbsp;Berrada holding that Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar is entitled to damages for
being deprived of the possibility of engaging in coffee roasting from 1986 due to such non-compete undertaking. At that time, the court appointed two experts to assess the amount of damages to be awarded. In December&nbsp;2003, these experts
delivered a report concluding that they could see no</FONT></TD>

<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="TOP"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2><BR>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
evidence of loss suffered by Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar. Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar has asked the court that this report be set aside and new court experts be appointed. On April&nbsp;15, 2004, the court delivered a judgment upholding the defenses of Kraft Foods Maroc and
rejecting the claims of Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar. Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar has not yet appealed this judgment. The existence of the claims of Mr.&nbsp;Gaouar was not disclosed by Mr.&nbsp;Berrada at the time of the Company's acquisition of Kraft Foods Maroc in 2001.
As a result, in the event that the Company is ultimately found liable on appeal for damages to plaintiff in this case, the Company believes that it may have claims against Mr.&nbsp;Berrada for recovery of all or a portion of the amount.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR VALIGN="TOP">

<TD COLSPAN=3><FONT SIZE=2><BR>
In May&nbsp;2001, the State of Ohio notified the Company that it may be subject to an enforcement action for alleged past violations of the Company's wastewater discharge permit at its production facility in Farmdale, Ohio. The State has offered to
attempt to negotiate a settlement of this matter, and the parties currently are involved in settlement negotiations.</FONT></TD>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="ja2832_item_5._other_information."> </A>
<A NAME="toc_ja2832_5"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Item&nbsp;5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other Information.    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. The Company's new segments are U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S.
Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America
reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously
reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's 2003 quarterly volume, net revenues and operating companies income under the new segment structure are as follows: </FONT></P>
